"""
worker/ir_physics/models.py
Immutable State Definitions for the JAX-GFL Physics Kernel.
Architecture: Periodic Torus Topology / RK4 Integration.
"""
import jax.numpy as jnp
from typing import NamedTuple

class SimState(NamedTuple):
    """
    The Single Source of Truth for the Simulation at Time T.
    """
    time_idx: int
    field: jnp.ndarray          # Complex Field A (The Matter) | Shape: (N, N, N)
    
    # --- Geometric Feedback Loop Tensors ---
    omega: jnp.ndarray          # Conformal Factor (The Geometry)
    grad_omega: jnp.ndarray     # Geometric Gradients (The Feedback)
    
    # --- Metrics ---
    h_norm: jnp.ndarray         # Hamiltonian Constraint Residual (Scalar Diagnostic)
    
    # --- Governance ---
    config_hash: int            # Provenance tracking (SHA1 proxy)

class SimParams(NamedTuple):
    """
    Static Parameters.
    Closed over by the JIT compiler.
    """
    dt: float                   # Time step size
    epsilon: float              # Linear growth coefficient
    
    # --- GFL Coupling Parameters ---
    alpha: float                # Geometric Coupling Strength (Exponent factor)
    rho_vac: float              # Vacuum Density Baseline
    
    # --- S-NCGL Parameters ---
    c1: float                   # Complex Diffusion coefficient
    c3: float                   # Nonlinear Phase Shift coefficient
    splash_fraction: float      # Strength of non-local interaction
    sigma_k: float              # Width of splash kernel
    dx: float                   # Grid spacing (usually 1.0)
2. worker/ir_physics/kernels.py
Implements jnp.roll for periodic gradients and the RK4 integrator.

Python
"""
worker/ir_physics/kernels.py
JIT-Compiled Geometric Feedback Loop (GFL) Logic.
Architecture: Periodic Torus (Roll-based) + RK4 Integrator.
"""
import jax
import jax.numpy as jnp
from .models import SimState, SimParams

@jax.jit
def get_green_function(shape, dx, sigma_k):
    """
    Precompute non-local Gaussian kernel (Splash Term).
    Periodic by definition (FFT).
    """
    kx = jnp.fft.fftfreq(shape[0], dx) * 2 * jnp.pi
    ky = jnp.fft.fftfreq(shape[1], dx) * 2 * jnp.pi
    kz = jnp.fft.fftfreq(shape[2], dx) * 2 * jnp.pi
    KX, KY, KZ = jnp.meshgrid(kx, ky, kz, indexing='ij')
    k2 = KX**2 + KY**2 + KZ**2
    return jnp.exp(-k2 * sigma_k)

def solve_geometry_proxy(rho, params):
    """
    Stage 3: Geometry Solver.
    Convention: Gravity Well.
    As Density (rho) Increases -> Omega Decreases (Space Contracts).
    """
    rho_safe = rho + 1e-9
    # Limit the compression ratio to prevent numerical singularities
    ratio = jnp.clip(params.rho_vac / rho_safe, 1e-4, 1e4)
    omega = jnp.power(ratio, params.alpha / 2.0)
    # Hard clamp to prevent total collapse (Black Hole Limit)
    return jnp.clip(omega, 0.01, 1.5)

def get_gradients_periodic(f, dx):
    """
    Central Difference Gradient on a Torus using Roll.
    df/dx ~ (f(x+1) - f(x-1)) / 2dx
    """
    gx = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=0) - jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=0)) / (2 * dx)
    gy = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=1) - jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=1)) / (2 * dx)
    gz = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=2) - jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=2)) / (2 * dx)
    return jnp.stack([gx, gy, gz], axis=-1)

def laplacian_periodic(f, dx):
    """
    Scalar Laplacian on a Torus using Roll.
    d2f/dx2 ~ (f(x+1) - 2f + f(x-1)) / dx^2
    """
    lx = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=0) - 2 * f + jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=0)) / (dx**2)
    ly = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=1) - 2 * f + jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=1)) / (dx**2)
    lz = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=2) - 2 * f + jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=2)) / (dx**2)
    return lx + ly + lz

def covariant_laplacian(field, omega, grad_omega, dx):
    """
    Stage 1: Covariant Evolution (Periodic).
    Implements Divergence Form:
    Box_g A = Omega^-2 * [ Laplacian(A) + (D-2)*(Grad(Omega)/Omega) . Grad(A) ]
    """
    D = 3.0
    
    # 1. Standard Laplacian (Periodic)
    lap = laplacian_periodic(field, dx)
    
    # 2. Gradient Coupling
    grad_A = get_gradients_periodic(field, dx)
    
    # Dot Product: sum(Grad_Omega * Grad_A) over the vector axis (last axis)
    dot_prod = jnp.sum(grad_omega * grad_A, axis=-1)
    
    # Coupling Term
    coupling = (D - 2.0) * (dot_prod / (omega + 1e-9))
    
    # 3. Total Box_g
    box_g = (1.0 / (omega**2 + 1e-9)) * (lap + coupling)
    return box_g

def compute_time_derivative(A, omega, grad_omega, params, splash_green_fn):
    """
    Calculates dA/dt for the S-NCGL system.
    Used by the RK4 integrator.
    """
    # 1. Density
    rho = jnp.abs(A)**2
    
    # 2. Covariant Diffusion (The "Real Space" Physics)
    diff_term = covariant_laplacian(A, omega, grad_omega, params.dx)
    linear_op = (1 + 1j * params.c1) * diff_term
    
    # 3. Nonlinear Saturation
    nonlinear = (1 + 1j * params.c3) * rho * A
    
    # 4. Splash (Spectral) - Non-local interaction
    A_k = jnp.fft.fftn(A)
    splash = jnp.fft.ifftn(A_k * splash_green_fn)
    
    # 5. Result
    dA_dt = (params.epsilon * A) + linear_op - nonlinear + (params.splash_fraction * splash)
    return dA_dt

def calculate_h_norm(omega, rho, params):
    """
    Diagnostic: How well does the proxy geometry match the Poisson source?
    This is NOT a constraint solver, just a check.
    H ~ Laplacian(Omega) + alpha * rho * Omega
    """
    lap_omega = laplacian_periodic(omega, params.dx)
    # We expect Laplacian(Omega) to balance the density source
    residual = lap_omega + (params.alpha * rho * omega)
    return jnp.sqrt(jnp.mean(jnp.abs(residual)**2))

@jax.jit
def step_physics(state: SimState, params: SimParams, splash_green_fn: jnp.ndarray) -> SimState:
    """
    Performs one time step using Runge-Kutta 4 (RK4) integration.
    """
    A0 = state.field
    dt = params.dt
    
    # --- Geometric Feedback Loop: Geometry is calculated from A0 ---
    # We use the T0 geometry for the entire T0 -> T1 RK4 transition.
    # This avoids re-solving geometry 4 times per step (expensive).
    
    rho0 = jnp.abs(A0)**2
    omega0 = solve_geometry_proxy(rho0, params)
    grad_omega0 = get_gradients_periodic(omega0, params.dx)
    
    # --- RK4 Integration ---
    
    # k1
    k1 = compute_time_derivative(A0, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)
    
    # k2
    k2 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + 0.5 * dt * k1, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)
    
    # k3
    k3 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + 0.5 * dt * k2, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)
    
    # k4
    k4 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + dt * k3, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)
    
    # Update Field
    A_new = A0 + (dt / 6.0) * (k1 + 2*k2 + 2*k3 + k4)
    
    # --- Finalize Next State ---
    # Re-calculate geometry for the *next* state to store it
    rho_new = jnp.abs(A_new)**2
    omega_new = solve_geometry_proxy(rho_new, params)
    grad_omega_new = get_gradients_periodic(omega_new, params.dx)
    h_norm_val = calculate_h_norm(omega_new, rho_new, params)
    
    return SimState(
        time_idx=state.time_idx + 1,
        field=A_new,
        omega=omega_new,
        grad_omega=grad_omega_new,
        h_norm=h_norm_val,
        config_hash=state.config_hash
    )
3. worker/ir_physics/solver.py
Compatible with the new kernel signature.

Python
"""
worker/ir_physics/solver.py
The Scanning Engine.
"""
import jax
from functools import partial
from .models import SimState, SimParams
from .kernels import step_physics, get_green_function

@partial(jax.jit, static_argnames=['total_steps', 'grid_size'])
def run_simulation_scan(
    initial_state: SimState, 
    params: SimParams, 
    total_steps: int,
    grid_size: int
):
    """
    Executes the full simulation trajectory.
    """
    
    # 1. Precompute static Green's function (FFT)
    splash_green_fn = get_green_function(
        (grid_size, grid_size, grid_size), 
        params.dx, 
        params.sigma_k
    )

    # 2. Define the Scan Body
    def scan_body(carry: SimState, _):
        new_state = step_physics(carry, params, splash_green_fn)
        return new_state, new_state.h_norm

    # 3. Execute Scan
    final_state, h_norm_history = jax.lax.scan(
        scan_body,
        initial_state,
        None,
        length=total_steps
    )
    
    return final_state, h_norm_history

The Single Source of Truth for the Simulation at Time T.

"""

worker/ir_physics/kernels.py

JIT-Compiled Geometric Feedback Loop (GFL) Logic.

Architecture: Periodic Torus (Roll-based) + RK4 Integrator.

"""import jaximport jax.numpy as jnpfrom .models import SimState, SimParams@jax.jitdef get_green_function(shape, dx, sigma_k):

"""

Precompute non-local Gaussian kernel (Splash Term).

Periodic by definition (FFT).

"""

kx = jnp.fft.fftfreq(shape[0], dx) * 2 * jnp.pi

ky = jnp.fft.fftfreq(shape[1], dx) * 2 * jnp.pi

kz = jnp.fft.fftfreq(shape[2], dx) * 2 * jnp.pi

KX, KY, KZ = jnp.meshgrid(kx, ky, kz, indexing='ij')

k2 = KX**2 + KY**2 + KZ**2

return jnp.exp(-k2 * sigma_k)def solve_geometry_proxy(rho, params):

"""

Stage 3: Geometry Solver.

Convention: Gravity Well.

As Density (rho) Increases -> Omega Decreases (Space Contracts).

"""

rho_safe = rho + 1e-9

# Limit the compression ratio to prevent numerical singularities

ratio = jnp.clip(params.rho_vac / rho_safe, 1e-4, 1e4)

omega = jnp.power(ratio, params.alpha / 2.0)

# Hard clamp to prevent total collapse (Black Hole Limit)

return jnp.clip(omega, 0.01, 1.5)def get_gradients_periodic(f, dx):

"""

Central Difference Gradient on a Torus using Roll.

df/dx ~ (f(x+1) - f(x-1)) / 2dx

"""

gx = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=0) - jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=0)) / (2 * dx)

gy = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=1) - jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=1)) / (2 * dx)

gz = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=2) - jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=2)) / (2 * dx)

return jnp.stack([gx, gy, gz], axis=-1)def laplacian_periodic(f, dx):

"""

Scalar Laplacian on a Torus using Roll.

d2f/dx2 ~ (f(x+1) - 2f + f(x-1)) / dx^2

"""

lx = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=0) - 2 * f + jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=0)) / (dx**2)

ly = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=1) - 2 * f + jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=1)) / (dx**2)

lz = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=2) - 2 * f + jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=2)) / (dx**2)

return lx + ly + lzdef covariant_laplacian(field, omega, grad_omega, dx):

"""

Stage 1: Covariant Evolution (Periodic).

Implements Divergence Form:

Box_g A = Omega^-2 * [ Laplacian(A) + (D-2)*(Grad(Omega)/Omega) . Grad(A) ]

"""

D = 3.0


# 1. Standard Laplacian (Periodic)

lap = laplacian_periodic(field, dx)


# 2. Gradient Coupling

grad_A = get_gradients_periodic(field, dx)


# Dot Product: sum(Grad_Omega * Grad_A) over the vector axis (last axis)

dot_prod = jnp.sum(grad_omega * grad_A, axis=-1)


# Coupling Term

coupling = (D - 2.0) * (dot_prod / (omega + 1e-9))


# 3. Total Box_g

box_g = (1.0 / (omega**2 + 1e-9)) * (lap + coupling)

return box_gdef compute_time_derivative(A, omega, grad_omega, params, splash_green_fn):

"""

Calculates dA/dt for the S-NCGL system.

Used by the RK4 integrator.

"""

# 1. Density

rho = jnp.abs(A)**2


# 2. Covariant Diffusion (The "Real Space" Physics)

diff_term = covariant_laplacian(A, omega, grad_omega, params.dx)

linear_op = (1 + 1j * params.c1) * diff_term


# 3. Nonlinear Saturation

nonlinear = (1 + 1j * params.c3) * rho * A


# 4. Splash (Spectral) - Non-local interaction

A_k = jnp.fft.fftn(A)

splash = jnp.fft.ifftn(A_k * splash_green_fn)


# 5. Result

dA_dt = (params.epsilon * A) + linear_op - nonlinear + (params.splash_fraction * splash)

return dA_dtdef calculate_h_norm(omega, rho, params):

"""

Diagnostic: How well does the proxy geometry match the Poisson source?

This is NOT a constraint solver, just a check.

H ~ Laplacian(Omega) + alpha * rho * Omega

"""

lap_omega = laplacian_periodic(omega, params.dx)

# We expect Laplacian(Omega) to balance the density source

residual = lap_omega + (params.alpha * rho * omega)

return jnp.sqrt(jnp.mean(jnp.abs(residual)**2))@jax.jitdef step_physics(state: SimState, params: SimParams, splash_green_fn: jnp.ndarray) -> SimState:

"""

Performs one time step using Runge-Kutta 4 (RK4) integration.

"""

A0 = state.field

dt = params.dt


# --- Geometric Feedback Loop: Geometry is calculated from A0 ---

# We use the T0 geometry for the entire T0 -> T1 RK4 transition.

# This avoids re-solving geometry 4 times per step (expensive).


rho0 = jnp.abs(A0)**2

omega0 = solve_geometry_proxy(rho0, params)

grad_omega0 = get_gradients_periodic(omega0, params.dx)


# --- RK4 Integration ---


# k1

k1 = compute_time_derivative(A0, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)


# k2

k2 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + 0.5 * dt * k1, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)


# k3

k3 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + 0.5 * dt * k2, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)


# k4

k4 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + dt * k3, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)


# Update Field

A_new = A0 + (dt / 6.0) * (k1 + 2*k2 + 2*k3 + k4)


# --- Finalize Next State ---

# Re-calculate geometry for the *next* state to store it

rho_new = jnp.abs(A_new)**2

omega_new = solve_geometry_proxy(rho_new, params)

grad_omega_new = get_gradients_periodic(omega_new, params.dx)

h_norm_val = calculate_h_norm(omega_new, rho_new, params)


return SimState(

time_idx=state.time_idx + 1,

field=A_new,

omega=omega_new,

grad_omega=grad_omega_new,

h_norm=h_norm_val,

config_hash=state.config_hash

)

"""

import jax.numpy as jnp

from typing import NamedTuple



class SimState(NamedTuple):

    """

    The Single Source of Truth for the Simulation at Time T.

    """

    time_idx: int

    field: jnp.ndarray          # Complex Field A (The Matter) | Shape: (N, N, N)

    

    # --- Geometric Feedback Loop Tensors ---

    omega: jnp.ndarray          # Conformal Factor (The Geometry)

    grad_omega: jnp.ndarray     # Geometric Gradients (The Feedback)

    

    # --- Metrics ---

    h_norm: jnp.ndarray         # Hamiltonian Constraint Residual (Scalar Diagnostic)

    

    # --- Governance ---

    config_hash: int            # Provenance tracking (SHA1 proxy)



class SimParams(NamedTuple):

    """

    Static Parameters.

    Closed over by the JIT compiler.

    """

    dt: float                   # Time step size

    epsilon: float              # Linear growth coefficient

    

    # --- GFL Coupling Parameters ---

    alpha: float                # Geometric Coupling Strength (Exponent factor)

    rho_vac: float              # Vacuum Density Baseline

    

    # --- S-NCGL Parameters ---

    c1: float                   # Complex Diffusion coefficient

    c3: float                   # Nonlinear Phase Shift coefficient

    splash_fraction: float      # Strength of non-local interaction

    sigma_k: float              # Width of splash kernel

    dx: float                   # Grid spacing (usually 1.0)

#### **2. `worker/ir_physics/kernels.py**`

```python

"""

worker/ir_physics/kernels.py

JIT-Compiled Geometric Feedback Loop (GFL) Logic.

Architecture: Periodic Torus (Roll-based) + RK4 Integrator.

"""

import jax

import jax.numpy as jnp

from .models import SimState, SimParams



@jax.jit

def get_green_function(shape, dx, sigma_k):

    """

    Precompute non-local Gaussian kernel (Splash Term).

    Periodic by definition (FFT).

    """

    kx = jnp.fft.fftfreq(shape[0], dx) * 2 * jnp.pi

    ky = jnp.fft.fftfreq(shape[1], dx) * 2 * jnp.pi

    kz = jnp.fft.fftfreq(shape[2], dx) * 2 * jnp.pi

    KX, KY, KZ = jnp.meshgrid(kx, ky, kz, indexing='ij')

    k2 = KX**2 + KY**2 + KZ**2

    return jnp.exp(-k2 * sigma_k)



def solve_geometry_proxy(rho, params):

    """

    Stage 3: Geometry Solver.

    Convention: Gravity Well.

    As Density (rho) Increases -> Omega Decreases (Space Contracts).

    """

    rho_safe = rho + 1e-9

    # Limit the compression ratio to prevent numerical singularities

    ratio = jnp.clip(params.rho_vac / rho_safe, 1e-4, 1e4)

    omega = jnp.power(ratio, params.alpha / 2.0)

    # Hard clamp to prevent total collapse (Black Hole Limit)

    return jnp.clip(omega, 0.01, 1.5)



def get_gradients_periodic(f, dx):

    """

    Central Difference Gradient on a Torus using Roll.

    df/dx ~ (f(x+1) - f(x-1)) / 2dx

    """

    gx = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=0) - jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=0)) / (2 * dx)

    gy = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=1) - jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=1)) / (2 * dx)

    gz = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=2) - jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=2)) / (2 * dx)

    return jnp.stack([gx, gy, gz], axis=-1)



def laplacian_periodic(f, dx):

    """

    Scalar Laplacian on a Torus using Roll.

    d2f/dx2 ~ (f(x+1) - 2f + f(x-1)) / dx^2

    """

    lx = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=0) - 2 * f + jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=0)) / (dx**2)

    ly = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=1) - 2 * f + jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=1)) / (dx**2)

    lz = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=2) - 2 * f + jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=2)) / (dx**2)

    return lx + ly + lz



def covariant_laplacian(field, omega, grad_omega, dx):

    """

    Stage 1: Covariant Evolution (Periodic).

    Implements Divergence Form:

    Box_g A = Omega^-2 * [ Laplacian(A) + (D-2)*(Grad(Omega)/Omega) . Grad(A) ]

    """

    D = 3.0

    

    # 1. Standard Laplacian (Periodic)

    lap = laplacian_periodic(field, dx)

    

    # 2. Gradient Coupling

    grad_A = get_gradients_periodic(field, dx)

    

    # Dot Product: sum(Grad_Omega * Grad_A) over the vector axis (last axis)

    dot_prod = jnp.sum(grad_omega * grad_A, axis=-1)

    

    # Coupling Term

    coupling = (D - 2.0) * (dot_prod / (omega + 1e-9))

    

    # 3. Total Box_g

    box_g = (1.0 / (omega**2 + 1e-9)) * (lap + coupling)

    return box_g



def compute_time_derivative(A, omega, grad_omega, params, splash_green_fn):

    """

    Calculates dA/dt for the S-NCGL system.

    Used by the RK4 integrator.

    """

    # 1. Density

    rho = jnp.abs(A)**2

    

    # 2. Covariant Diffusion (The "Real Space" Physics)

    diff_term = covariant_laplacian(A, omega, grad_omega, params.dx)

    linear_op = (1 + 1j * params.c1) * diff_term

    

    # 3. Nonlinear Saturation

    nonlinear = (1 + 1j * params.c3) * rho * A

    

    # 4. Splash (Spectral) - Non-local interaction

    A_k = jnp.fft.fftn(A)

    splash = jnp.fft.ifftn(A_k * splash_green_fn)

    

    # 5. Result

    dA_dt = (params.epsilon * A) + linear_op - nonlinear + (params.splash_fraction * splash)

    return dA_dt



def calculate_h_norm(omega, rho, params):

    """

    Diagnostic: How well does the proxy geometry match the Poisson source?

    This is NOT a constraint solver, just a check.

    H ~ Laplacian(Omega) + alpha * rho * Omega

    """

    lap_omega = laplacian_periodic(omega, params.dx)

    # We expect Laplacian(Omega) to balance the density source

    residual = lap_omega + (params.alpha * rho * omega)

    return jnp.sqrt(jnp.mean(jnp.abs(residual)**2))



@jax.jit

def step_physics(state: SimState, params: SimParams, splash_green_fn: jnp.ndarray) -> SimState:

    """

    Performs one time step using Runge-Kutta 4 (RK4) integration.

    """

    A0 = state.field

    dt = params.dt

    

    # --- Geometric Feedback Loop: Geometry is calculated from A0 ---

    # We use the T0 geometry for the entire T0 -> T1 RK4 transition.

    # This avoids re-solving geometry 4 times per step (expensive).

    

    rho0 = jnp.abs(A0)**2

    omega0 = solve_geometry_proxy(rho0, params)

    grad_omega0 = get_gradients_periodic(omega0, params.dx)

    

    # --- RK4 Integration ---

    

    # k1

    k1 = compute_time_derivative(A0, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)

    

    # k2

    k2 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + 0.5 * dt * k1, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)

    

    # k3

    k3 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + 0.5 * dt * k2, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)

    

    # k4

    k4 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + dt * k3, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)

    

    # Update Field

    A_new = A0 + (dt / 6.0) * (k1 + 2*k2 + 2*k3 + k4)

    

    # --- Finalize Next State ---

    # Re-calculate geometry for the *next* state to store it

    rho_new = jnp.abs(A_new)**2

    omega_new = solve_geometry_proxy(rho_new, params)

    grad_omega_new = get_gradients_periodic(omega_new, params.dx)

    h_norm_val = calculate_h_norm(omega_new, rho_new, params)

    

    return SimState(

        time_idx=state.time_idx + 1,

        field=A_new,

        omega=omega_new,

        grad_omega=grad_omega_new,

        h_norm=h_norm_val,

        config_hash=state.config_hash

    )



```



#### **3. `worker/ir_physics/solver.py**`



Compatible with the new kernel signature.



```python

"""

worker/ir_physics/solver.py

The Scanning Engine.

"""

import jax

from functools import partial

from .models import SimState, SimParams

from .kernels import step_physics, get_green_function



@partial(jax.jit, static_argnames=['total_steps', 'grid_size'])

def run_simulation_scan(

    initial_state: SimState, 

    params: SimParams, 

    total_steps: int,

    grid_size: int

):

    """

    Executes the full simulation trajectory.

    """

    

    # 1. Precompute static Green's function (FFT)

    splash_green_fn = get_green_function(

        (grid_size, grid_size, grid_size), 

        params.dx, 

        params.sigma_k

    )



    # 2. Define the Scan Body

    def scan_body(carry: SimState, _):

        new_state = step_physics(carry, params, splash_green_fn)

        return new_state, new_state.h_norm



    # 3. Execute Scan

    final_state, h_norm_history = jax.lax.scan(

        scan_body,

        initial_state,

        None,

        length=total_steps

    )

    

    return final_state, h_norm_history



```

"""
worker/ir_physics/models.py
Immutable State Definitions for the JAX-GFL Physics Kernel.
Architecture: Periodic Torus Topology / RK4 Integration.
"""
import jax.numpy as jnp
from typing import NamedTuple

class SimState(NamedTuple):
    """
    The Single Source of Truth for the Simulation at Time T.
    """
    time_idx: int
    field: jnp.ndarray          # Complex Field A (The Matter) | Shape: (N, N, N)
    
    # --- Geometric Feedback Loop Tensors ---
    omega: jnp.ndarray          # Conformal Factor (The Geometry)
    grad_omega: jnp.ndarray     # Geometric Gradients (The Feedback)
    
    # --- Metrics ---
    h_norm: jnp.ndarray         # Hamiltonian Constraint Residual (Scalar Diagnostic)
    
    # --- Governance ---
    config_hash: int            # Provenance tracking (SHA1 proxy)

class SimParams(NamedTuple):
    """
    Static Parameters.
    Closed over by the JIT compiler.
    """
    dt: float                   # Time step size
    epsilon: float              # Linear growth coefficient
    
    # --- GFL Coupling Parameters ---
    alpha: float                # Geometric Coupling Strength (Exponent factor)
    rho_vac: float              # Vacuum Density Baseline
    
    # --- S-NCGL Parameters ---
    c1: float                   # Complex Diffusion coefficient
    c3: float                   # Nonlinear Phase Shift coefficient
    splash_fraction: float      # Strength of non-local interaction
    sigma_k: float              # Width of splash kernel
    dx: float                   # Grid spacing (usually 1.0)
2. worker/ir_physics/kernels.py
Implements jnp.roll for periodic gradients and the RK4 integrator.

Python
"""
worker/ir_physics/kernels.py
JIT-Compiled Geometric Feedback Loop (GFL) Logic.
Architecture: Periodic Torus (Roll-based) + RK4 Integrator.
"""
import jax
import jax.numpy as jnp
from .models import SimState, SimParams

@jax.jit
def get_green_function(shape, dx, sigma_k):
    """
    Precompute non-local Gaussian kernel (Splash Term).
    Periodic by definition (FFT).
    """
    kx = jnp.fft.fftfreq(shape[0], dx) * 2 * jnp.pi
    ky = jnp.fft.fftfreq(shape[1], dx) * 2 * jnp.pi
    kz = jnp.fft.fftfreq(shape[2], dx) * 2 * jnp.pi
    KX, KY, KZ = jnp.meshgrid(kx, ky, kz, indexing='ij')
    k2 = KX**2 + KY**2 + KZ**2
    return jnp.exp(-k2 * sigma_k)

def solve_geometry_proxy(rho, params):
    """
    Stage 3: Geometry Solver.
    Convention: Gravity Well.
    As Density (rho) Increases -> Omega Decreases (Space Contracts).
    """
    rho_safe = rho + 1e-9
    # Limit the compression ratio to prevent numerical singularities
    ratio = jnp.clip(params.rho_vac / rho_safe, 1e-4, 1e4)
    omega = jnp.power(ratio, params.alpha / 2.0)
    # Hard clamp to prevent total collapse (Black Hole Limit)
    return jnp.clip(omega, 0.01, 1.5)

def get_gradients_periodic(f, dx):
    """
    Central Difference Gradient on a Torus using Roll.
    df/dx ~ (f(x+1) - f(x-1)) / 2dx
    """
    gx = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=0) - jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=0)) / (2 * dx)
    gy = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=1) - jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=1)) / (2 * dx)
    gz = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=2) - jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=2)) / (2 * dx)
    return jnp.stack([gx, gy, gz], axis=-1)

def laplacian_periodic(f, dx):
    """
    Scalar Laplacian on a Torus using Roll.
    d2f/dx2 ~ (f(x+1) - 2f + f(x-1)) / dx^2
    """
    lx = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=0) - 2 * f + jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=0)) / (dx**2)
    ly = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=1) - 2 * f + jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=1)) / (dx**2)
    lz = (jnp.roll(f, -1, axis=2) - 2 * f + jnp.roll(f, 1, axis=2)) / (dx**2)
    return lx + ly + lz

def covariant_laplacian(field, omega, grad_omega, dx):
    """
    Stage 1: Covariant Evolution (Periodic).
    Implements Divergence Form:
    Box_g A = Omega^-2 * [ Laplacian(A) + (D-2)*(Grad(Omega)/Omega) . Grad(A) ]
    """
    D = 3.0
    
    # 1. Standard Laplacian (Periodic)
    lap = laplacian_periodic(field, dx)
    
    # 2. Gradient Coupling
    grad_A = get_gradients_periodic(field, dx)
    
    # Dot Product: sum(Grad_Omega * Grad_A) over the vector axis (last axis)
    dot_prod = jnp.sum(grad_omega * grad_A, axis=-1)
    
    # Coupling Term
    coupling = (D - 2.0) * (dot_prod / (omega + 1e-9))
    
    # 3. Total Box_g
    box_g = (1.0 / (omega**2 + 1e-9)) * (lap + coupling)
    return box_g

def compute_time_derivative(A, omega, grad_omega, params, splash_green_fn):
    """
    Calculates dA/dt for the S-NCGL system.
    Used by the RK4 integrator.
    """
    # 1. Density
    rho = jnp.abs(A)**2
    
    # 2. Covariant Diffusion (The "Real Space" Physics)
    diff_term = covariant_laplacian(A, omega, grad_omega, params.dx)
    linear_op = (1 + 1j * params.c1) * diff_term
    
    # 3. Nonlinear Saturation
    nonlinear = (1 + 1j * params.c3) * rho * A
    
    # 4. Splash (Spectral) - Non-local interaction
    A_k = jnp.fft.fftn(A)
    splash = jnp.fft.ifftn(A_k * splash_green_fn)
    
    # 5. Result
    dA_dt = (params.epsilon * A) + linear_op - nonlinear + (params.splash_fraction * splash)
    return dA_dt

def calculate_h_norm(omega, rho, params):
    """
    Diagnostic: How well does the proxy geometry match the Poisson source?
    This is NOT a constraint solver, just a check.
    H ~ Laplacian(Omega) + alpha * rho * Omega
    """
    lap_omega = laplacian_periodic(omega, params.dx)
    # We expect Laplacian(Omega) to balance the density source
    residual = lap_omega + (params.alpha * rho * omega)
    return jnp.sqrt(jnp.mean(jnp.abs(residual)**2))

@jax.jit
def step_physics(state: SimState, params: SimParams, splash_green_fn: jnp.ndarray) -> SimState:
    """
    Performs one time step using Runge-Kutta 4 (RK4) integration.
    """
    A0 = state.field
    dt = params.dt
    
    # --- Geometric Feedback Loop: Geometry is calculated from A0 ---
    # We use the T0 geometry for the entire T0 -> T1 RK4 transition.
    # This avoids re-solving geometry 4 times per step (expensive).
    
    rho0 = jnp.abs(A0)**2
    omega0 = solve_geometry_proxy(rho0, params)
    grad_omega0 = get_gradients_periodic(omega0, params.dx)
    
    # --- RK4 Integration ---
    
    # k1
    k1 = compute_time_derivative(A0, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)
    
    # k2
    k2 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + 0.5 * dt * k1, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)
    
    # k3
    k3 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + 0.5 * dt * k2, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)
    
    # k4
    k4 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + dt * k3, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)
    
    # Update Field
    A_new = A0 + (dt / 6.0) * (k1 + 2*k2 + 2*k3 + k4)
    
    # --- Finalize Next State ---
    # Re-calculate geometry for the *next* state to store it
    rho_new = jnp.abs(A_new)**2
    omega_new = solve_geometry_proxy(rho_new, params)
    grad_omega_new = get_gradients_periodic(omega_new, params.dx)
    h_norm_val = calculate_h_norm(omega_new, rho_new, params)
    
    return SimState(
        time_idx=state.time_idx + 1,
        field=A_new,
        omega=omega_new,
        grad_omega=grad_omega_new,
        h_norm=h_norm_val,
        config_hash=state.config_hash
    )
3. worker/ir_physics/solver.py
Compatible with the new kernel signature.

Python
"""
worker/ir_physics/solver.py
The Scanning Engine.
"""
import jax
from functools import partial
from .models import SimState, SimParams
from .kernels import step_physics, get_green_function

@partial(jax.jit, static_argnames=['total_steps', 'grid_size'])
def run_simulation_scan(
    initial_state: SimState, 
    params: SimParams, 
    total_steps: int,
    grid_size: int
):
    """
    Executes the full simulation trajectory.
    """
    
    # 1. Precompute static Green's function (FFT)
    splash_green_fn = get_green_function(
        (grid_size, grid_size, grid_size), 
        params.dx, 
        params.sigma_k
    )

    # 2. Define the Scan Body
    def scan_body(carry: SimState, _):
        new_state = step_physics(carry, params, splash_green_fn)
        return new_state, new_state.h_norm

    # 3. Execute Scan
    final_state, h_norm_history = jax.lax.scan(
        scan_body,
        initial_state,
        None,
        length=total_steps
    )
    
    return final_state, h_norm_history
Formal Justification
Here is the engineering defense for this architecture.

1. Mathematical Consistency: The "Topology Imperative"
Choice: jnp.roll (Toroidal/Periodic) over jax.scipy.signal.convolve (Zero-Padding).

The Conflict: Your simulation utilizes a Spectral "Splash" term (FFT-based). Mathematically, an FFT assumes the domain is a Torus—waves leaving the right side re-enter the left.

The Problem with Convolution: Standard convolution stencils typically assume "Zero Padding" (dead space) at the boundaries. If we mixed FFT Splash (Infinite Loop) with Zero-Padded Derivatives (Walls), the physics engine would generate "Phantom Gravity"—artificial gradients at the edges of the simulation box where the two topologies conflict.

The Solution: jnp.roll enforces a periodic boundary condition for the derivatives (∂ 
x
​
 ,∇ 
2
 ). This aligns the "Field Topology" perfectly with the "Splash Topology," ensuring the universe is seamless and valid at every voxel, not just the center.

2. Numerical Stability: Solving the "Stiffness" Problem
Choice: Runge-Kutta 4 (RK4) over Euler Integration.

The Physics: We are modeling "Gravity Wells" using an algebraic proxy: Ω=(ρ 
vac
​
 /ρ) 
α/2
 . As density (ρ) spikes, Ω approaches zero.

The Math: The Covariant D'Alembertian contains terms divided by Ω (e.g., 1/Ω 
2
 ). When Ω gets small, these terms become huge. This creates "Stiff Differential Equations."

The Failure Mode: A simple Euler integrator (linear extrapolation) cannot handle the sharp curves of a stiff equation; it overshoots the curve, creating massive energy spikes and NaN values.

The Solution: RK4 samples the curvature of the field four times per time-step (k 
1

 ,k

​
 ,k 
3

 ,k 
4

 ). This allows the solver to "navigate" the steep curves of the gravity well without crashing, enabling us to simulate deep gravitational attractors that would otherwise destroy the simulation.

3. Hardware Constraints: The GTX 1080 Reality

Memory Bandwidth: A GTX 1080 has 8GB of VRAM.

 ,K 
ij

 ,α,β

 ,Γ

 ) or larger batch sizes.

Compute Efficiency: jnp.roll compiles down to simple pointer arithmetic in XLA (JAX's compiler). It avoids the overhead of constructing complex convolution matrix buffers, making it significantly faster on the Pascal architecture of the GTX 1080.

Choice: Algebraic Proxy with h_norm Monitoring over Elliptic Constraint Solving.

The Trade-off: Solving the Elliptic Constraint Equation (∇

• ρ_max ↑

• G_max ↑ exponentially in α

• total_radius ↑

• dt automatically shrinks

This prevents gravity-well blowup without artificial Ω clamping.

Do NOT make dt a JAX dynamic Python variable.

Pass dt_adaptive as a computed scalar into RK4

Keep it inside the JIT trace

Otherwise you’ll break XLA compilation.

PHASE 1 — Optional SDG Spectral Comparison Mode

Goal:

1️⃣ Define the SDG Constraint

We assume SDG elliptic form:



∇2Ω+𝛼𝜌Ω=0

∇2

Ω+αρΩ=0

In Fourier space:



−𝑘2Ω𝑘+𝛼(𝜌Ω)𝑘=0

−k2

Ωk

​+α(ρΩ)k

​=0

But this is nonlinear because of ρΩ.

For Phase 1 comparison mode, we linearize:

Assume weak coupling:



∇2Ω+𝛼𝜌=0

∇2

Ω+αρ=0

This gives spectral solve:



Ω𝑘=𝛼𝜌𝑘𝑘2(𝑘≠0)

Ωk

​=k2

αρk

​

​(k

=0)

We set:



Ω𝑘=0=1

Ωk=0

​=1

to preserve normalization.

2️⃣ Implement Spectral SDG Solve (Periodic Domain)

Add optional function:





def solve_geometry_sdg_spectral(rho, alpha, dx):

N = rho.shape[0]


kx = jnp.fft.fftfreq(N, dx) * 2 * jnp.pi

ky = jnp.fft.fftfreq(N, dx) * 2 * jnp.pi

kz = jnp.fft.fftfreq(N, dx) * 2 * jnp.pi


KX, KY, KZ = jnp.meshgrid(kx, ky, kz, indexing='ij')

k2 = KX**2 + KY**2 + KZ**2


rho_k = jnp.fft.fftn(rho)


# Avoid divide-by-zero at k=0

omega_k = jnp.where(

k2 > 0,

alpha * rho_k / k2,

1.0 + 0j

)


omega_sdg = jnp.real(jnp.fft.ifftn(omega_k))


return omega_sdg

3️⃣ Comparison Metric

At chosen interval (e.g. every 50 steps):





omega_proxy = omega_new

omega_sdg = solve_geometry_sdg_spectral(rho_new, alpha, dx)



sdg_mismatch = jnp.sqrt(jnp.mean((omega_proxy - omega_sdg)**2))

Track:

• h_norm

• sdg_mismatch

If mismatch grows, algebraic proxy deviates strongly from elliptic geometry.

This tells you:

Where your scalar gravity approximation breaks down.

4️⃣ Important

Do NOT use SDG solve inside RK4.

Only use as comparison.

Otherwise you'll reintroduce stiffness.

Loop across grid sizes:





for N in [64, 96, 128]:

dx = L / N

dt = base_dt * (dx / dx_ref)**2


run_simulation(N, dx, dt)


collect_metrics()

Important:

dt must scale ∝ dx²

Otherwise resolution test is invalid.

𝐸𝑁=L2 difference between spectra at N and 2N

𝐸2𝑁≈14𝐸𝑁

You're seeing resolution-dependent artifacts.

"""

worker/ir_physics/kernels.py

GFL-RK4 Physics Core

Extended with:

- Explicit spectral radius dt bound

- Splash contribution

- Curvature-adaptive dt

- α_critical estimator

- Optional SDG spectral comparison

"""import jaximport jax.numpy as jnpfrom .models import SimState, SimParams# ============================================================# PERIODIC DIFFERENTIAL OPERATORS (Toroidal Topology)# ============================================================def get_gradients_periodic(f, dx):

gx = (jnp.roll(f, -1, 0) - jnp.roll(f, 1, 0)) / (2 * dx)

gy = (jnp.roll(f, -1, 1) - jnp.roll(f, 1, 1)) / (2 * dx)

gz = (jnp.roll(f, -1, 2) - jnp.roll(f, 1, 2)) / (2 * dx)

return jnp.stack([gx, gy, gz], axis=-1)def laplacian_periodic(f, dx):

lx = (jnp.roll(f, -1, 0) - 2*f + jnp.roll(f, 1, 0)) / dx**2

ly = (jnp.roll(f, -1, 1) - 2*f + jnp.roll(f, 1, 1)) / dx**2

lz = (jnp.roll(f, -1, 2) - 2*f + jnp.roll(f, 1, 2)) / dx**2

return lx + ly + lz# ============================================================# GEOMETRY# ============================================================def solve_geometry_proxy(rho, params):

rho_safe = rho + 1e-9

ratio = jnp.clip(params.rho_vac / rho_safe, 1e-4, 1e4)

omega = ratio ** (params.alpha / 2.0)

return jnp.clip(omega, 0.01, 1.5)# ============================================================# STABILITY ANALYSIS TOOLS# ============================================================def spectral_radius_estimate(params: SimParams, rho_max: float):

"""

Spectral radius of linear operator including splash.

"""



# minimum omega (worst curvature compression)

omega_min = jnp.clip(

(params.rho_vac / (rho_max + 1e-9)) ** (params.alpha / 2.0),

0.01, 1.5

)



curvature_amp = 1.0 / (omega_min**2 + 1e-9)



# Laplacian spectral radius (3D periodic)

k_max = jnp.pi / params.dx

lap_radius = 6.0 * k_max**2 # conservative bound



splash_radius = params.splash_fraction



total_radius = curvature_amp * lap_radius + splash_radius



return total_radiusdef dt_stability_bound(params: SimParams, rho_max: float):

"""

RK4 stability: |λ dt| < ~2.8

"""

radius = spectral_radius_estimate(params, rho_max)

return 2.8 / (radius + 1e-9)def adaptive_dt(params: SimParams, rho):

"""

Curvature-adaptive dt scaling

"""

rho_max = jnp.max(rho)

return dt_stability_bound(params, rho_max)def alpha_critical(params: SimParams, rho_max: float):

"""

Solve dt = dt_bound for alpha.

Approximate analytical inversion.

"""



k_max = jnp.pi / params.dx

lap_radius = 6.0 * k_max**2



# rearranged stability inequality

# dt * ( (rho_max/rho_vac)^alpha * lap_radius ) ≈ 2.8



ratio = rho_max / params.rho_vac

target = 2.8 / (params.dt * lap_radius)



# log solve

alpha = jnp.log(target) / jnp.log(ratio + 1e-9)



return jnp.maximum(alpha, 0.0)# ============================================================# COVARIANT OPERATOR# ============================================================def covariant_laplacian(field, omega, grad_omega, dx):

D = 3.0

lap = laplacian_periodic(field, dx)

grad_A = get_gradients_periodic(field, dx)

dot_prod = jnp.sum(grad_omega * grad_A, axis=-1)

coupling = (D - 2.0) * (dot_prod / (omega + 1e-9))

return (lap + coupling) / (omega**2 + 1e-9)# ============================================================# TIME EVOLUTION# ============================================================def compute_time_derivative(A, omega, grad_omega, params, splash_green_fn):

rho = jnp.abs(A)**2



diff_term = covariant_laplacian(A, omega, grad_omega, params.dx)

linear_op = (1 + 1j * params.c1) * diff_term



nonlinear = (1 + 1j * params.c3) * rho * A



A_k = jnp.fft.fftn(A)

splash = jnp.fft.ifftn(A_k * splash_green_fn)



return (params.epsilon * A) + linear_op - nonlinear + (params.splash_fraction * splash)def calculate_h_norm(omega, rho, params):

lap_omega = laplacian_periodic(omega, params.dx)

residual = lap_omega + (params.alpha * rho * omega)

return jnp.sqrt(jnp.mean(jnp.abs(residual)**2))# ============================================================# RK4 STEP# ============================================================@jax.jitdef step_physics(state: SimState, params: SimParams, splash_green_fn):

A0 = state.field

dt = params.dt



rho0 = jnp.abs(A0)**2

omega0 = solve_geometry_proxy(rho0, params)

grad_omega0 = get_gradients_periodic(omega0, params.dx)



k1 = compute_time_derivative(A0, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)

k2 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + 0.5 * dt * k1, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)

k3 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + 0.5 * dt * k2, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)

k4 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + dt * k3, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)



A_new = A0 + (dt / 6.0) * (k1 + 2*k2 + 2*k3 + k4)



rho_new = jnp.abs(A_new)**2

omega_new = solve_geometry_proxy(rho_new, params)

grad_omega_new = get_gradients_periodic(omega_new, params.dx)



h_norm_val = calculate_h_norm(omega_new, rho_new, params)



return SimState(

time_idx=state.time_idx + 1,

field=A_new,

omega=omega_new,

grad_omega=grad_omega_new,

h_norm=h_norm_val,

config_hash=state.config_hash

)

2️⃣ NONLINEAR STABILITY ENVELOPE MAPPER

Create a new file:



worker/ir_physics/stability_envelope.py



import jax.numpy as jnpfrom .kernels import dt_stability_bound, alpha_criticaldef compute_stability_envelope(params, rho_range, alpha_range):

"""

Maps (alpha, rho_max) -> dt_bound

"""



dt_map = jnp.zeros((len(alpha_range), len(rho_range)))



for i, alpha in enumerate(alpha_range):

p = params._replace(alpha=float(alpha))

for j, rho in enumerate(rho_range):

dt_map = dt_map.at[i, j].set(dt_stability_bound(p, rho))



return dt_mapdef compute_alpha_critical_curve(params, rho_range):

curve = []

for rho in rho_range:

curve.append(alpha_critical(params, rho))

return jnp.array(curve)

def sdg_spectral_compare(A):

"""

Returns spectral energy distribution for SDG comparison mode.

"""

A_k = jnp.fft.fftn(A)

energy = jnp.abs(A_k)**2

return jnp.mean(energy, axis=(1,2))

You can call this optionally after simulation to compare SDG vs GFL spectral content.

1. worker/ir_physics/models.py
Defines the immutable state and parameters. Explicitly carries grad_omega for the feedback loop.

Python
"""
worker/ir_physics/models.py
Immutable State Definitions for the JAX-GFL Physics Kernel.
Architecture: Periodic Torus Topology / RK4 Integration.
"""
import jax.numpy as jnp
from typing import NamedTuple

class SimState(NamedTuple):
    """
    The Single Source of Truth for the Simulation at Time T.
    Passed through jax.lax.scan as the 'carry'.
    """
    time_idx: int
    field: jnp.ndarray          # Complex Field A (The Matter) | Shape: (N, N, N)
    
    # --- Geometric Feedback Loop Tensors ---
    omega: jnp.ndarray          # Conformal Factor (The Geometry)
    grad_omega: jnp.ndarray     # Geometric Gradients (The Feedback)
    
    # --- Metrics ---
    h_norm: jnp.ndarray         # Hamiltonian Constraint Residual (Scalar Diagnostic)
    
    # --- Governance ---
    config_hash: int            # Provenance tracking (SHA1 proxy)

class SimParams(NamedTuple):
    """
    Static Parameters.
    Closed over by the JIT compiler.
    """
    dt: float                   # Time step size
    epsilon: float              # Linear growth coefficient
    
    # --- GFL Coupling Parameters ---
    alpha: float                # Geometric Coupling Strength (Exponent factor)
    rho_vac: float              # Vacuum Density Baseline
    
    # --- S-NCGL Parameters ---
    c1: float                   # Complex Diffusion coefficient
    c3: float                   # Nonlinear Phase Shift coefficient
    splash_fraction: float      # Strength of non-local interaction
    sigma_k: float              # Width of splash kernel
    dx: float                   # Grid spacing (usually 1.0)
2. worker/ir_physics/kernels.py
The core physics engine. Includes RK4 integration, Periodic (Roll) Operators, and the new Stability Analysis tools (dt_stability_bound, alpha_critical).

Python
"""
worker/ir_physics/kernels.py
GFL-RK4 Physics Core
Extended with:
- Explicit spectral radius dt bound
- Splash contribution
- Curvature-adaptive dt
- α_critical estimator
- Optional SDG spectral comparison
"""
import jax
import jax.numpy as jnp
from .models import SimState, SimParams

# ============================================================
# SPECTRAL UTILS
# ============================================================
@jax.jit
def get_green_function(shape, dx, sigma_k):
    """
    Precompute non-local Gaussian kernel (Splash Term).
    Periodic by definition (FFT).
    """
    kx = jnp.fft.fftfreq(shape[0], dx) * 2 * jnp.pi
    ky = jnp.fft.fftfreq(shape[1], dx) * 2 * jnp.pi
    kz = jnp.fft.fftfreq(shape[2], dx) * 2 * jnp.pi
    KX, KY, KZ = jnp.meshgrid(kx, ky, kz, indexing='ij')
    k2 = KX**2 + KY**2 + KZ**2
    return jnp.exp(-k2 * sigma_k)

# ============================================================
# PERIODIC DIFFERENTIAL OPERATORS (Toroidal Topology)
# ============================================================
def get_gradients_periodic(f, dx):
    """
    Central Difference Gradient on a Torus using Roll.
    df/dx ~ (f(x+1) - f(x-1)) / 2dx
    """
    gx = (jnp.roll(f, -1, 0) - jnp.roll(f, 1, 0)) / (2 * dx)
    gy = (jnp.roll(f, -1, 1) - jnp.roll(f, 1, 1)) / (2 * dx)
    gz = (jnp.roll(f, -1, 2) - jnp.roll(f, 1, 2)) / (2 * dx)
    return jnp.stack([gx, gy, gz], axis=-1)

def laplacian_periodic(f, dx):
    """
    Scalar Laplacian on a Torus using Roll.
    d2f/dx2 ~ (f(x+1) - 2f + f(x-1)) / dx^2
    """
    lx = (jnp.roll(f, -1, 0) - 2*f + jnp.roll(f, 1, 0)) / dx**2
    ly = (jnp.roll(f, -1, 1) - 2*f + jnp.roll(f, 1, 1)) / dx**2
    lz = (jnp.roll(f, -1, 2) - 2*f + jnp.roll(f, 1, 2)) / dx**2
    return lx + ly + lz

# ============================================================
# GEOMETRY
# ============================================================
def solve_geometry_proxy(rho, params):
    """
    Algebraic Proxy: Omega = (rho_vac / rho)^(alpha/2)
    """
    rho_safe = rho + 1e-9
    ratio = jnp.clip(params.rho_vac / rho_safe, 1e-4, 1e4)
    omega = ratio ** (params.alpha / 2.0)
    return jnp.clip(omega, 0.01, 1.5)

# ============================================================
# STABILITY ANALYSIS TOOLS
# ============================================================
def spectral_radius_estimate(params: SimParams, rho_max: float):
    """
    Spectral radius of linear operator including splash.
    Used to estimate safe dt.
    """
    # minimum omega (worst curvature compression)
    omega_min = jnp.clip(
        (params.rho_vac / (rho_max + 1e-9)) ** (params.alpha / 2.0),
        0.01, 1.5
    )

    curvature_amp = 1.0 / (omega_min**2 + 1e-9)

    # Laplacian spectral radius (3D periodic)
    k_max = jnp.pi / params.dx
    lap_radius = 6.0 * k_max**2   # conservative bound (1/dx^2 factor implied in k_max logic or explicit)
    # Actually for finite difference L ~ 4/dx^2 per dim -> 12/dx^2 total
    lap_radius_fd = 12.0 / (params.dx**2)

    splash_radius = params.splash_fraction

    # Total radius estimate
    total_radius = curvature_amp * lap_radius_fd + splash_radius

    return total_radius

def dt_stability_bound(params: SimParams, rho_max: float):
    """
    RK4 stability: |λ dt| < ~2.8
    """
    radius = spectral_radius_estimate(params, rho_max)
    return 2.8 / (radius + 1e-9)

def adaptive_dt(params: SimParams, rho):
    """
    Curvature-adaptive dt scaling
    """
    rho_max = jnp.max(rho)
    return dt_stability_bound(params, rho_max)

def alpha_critical(params: SimParams, rho_max: float):
    """
    Solve dt = dt_bound for alpha.
    Approximate analytical inversion to find critical coupling.
    """
    # Laplacian contribution
    lap_radius_fd = 12.0 / (params.dx**2)

    # We want: dt * ( (rho_max/rho_vac)^alpha * lap_radius ) ≈ 2.8
    # (Assuming curvature dominates splash)
    
    ratio = rho_max / params.rho_vac
    target = 2.8 / (params.dt * lap_radius_fd)

    # log solve: alpha = ln(target) / ln(ratio)
    alpha = jnp.log(target) / jnp.log(ratio + 1e-9)

    return jnp.maximum(alpha, 0.0)

# ============================================================
# COVARIANT OPERATOR
# ============================================================
def covariant_laplacian(field, omega, grad_omega, dx):
    """
    Box_g A = Omega^-2 * [ Laplacian(A) + (D-2)*(Grad(Omega)/Omega) . Grad(A) ]
    """
    D = 3.0
    lap = laplacian_periodic(field, dx)
    grad_A = get_gradients_periodic(field, dx)
    
    dot_prod = jnp.sum(grad_omega * grad_A, axis=-1)
    coupling = (D - 2.0) * (dot_prod / (omega + 1e-9))
    
    return (lap + coupling) / (omega**2 + 1e-9)

# ============================================================
# TIME EVOLUTION
# ============================================================
def compute_time_derivative(A, omega, grad_omega, params, splash_green_fn):
    rho = jnp.abs(A)**2

    diff_term = covariant_laplacian(A, omega, grad_omega, params.dx)
    linear_op = (1 + 1j * params.c1) * diff_term

    nonlinear = (1 + 1j * params.c3) * rho * A

    A_k = jnp.fft.fftn(A)
    splash = jnp.fft.ifftn(A_k * splash_green_fn)

    return (params.epsilon * A) + linear_op - nonlinear + (params.splash_fraction * splash)

def calculate_h_norm(omega, rho, params):
    """
    Diagnostic: H ~ Laplacian(Omega) + alpha * rho * Omega
    """
    lap_omega = laplacian_periodic(omega, params.dx)
    residual = lap_omega + (params.alpha * rho * omega)
    return jnp.sqrt(jnp.mean(jnp.abs(residual)**2))

# ============================================================
# RK4 STEP
# ============================================================
@jax.jit
def step_physics(state: SimState, params: SimParams, splash_green_fn: jnp.ndarray) -> SimState:
    A0 = state.field
    dt = params.dt
    
    # 1. Geometry at T0 (Frozen for RK4 substeps)
    rho0 = jnp.abs(A0)**2
    omega0 = solve_geometry_proxy(rho0, params)
    grad_omega0 = get_gradients_periodic(omega0, params.dx)

    # 2. RK4 Integration
    k1 = compute_time_derivative(A0, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)
    k2 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + 0.5 * dt * k1, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)
    k3 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + 0.5 * dt * k2, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)
    k4 = compute_time_derivative(A0 + dt * k3, omega0, grad_omega0, params, splash_green_fn)

    A_new = A0 + (dt / 6.0) * (k1 + 2*k2 + 2*k3 + k4)

    # 3. Finalize Next State
    rho_new = jnp.abs(A_new)**2
    omega_new = solve_geometry_proxy(rho_new, params)
    grad_omega_new = get_gradients_periodic(omega_new, params.dx)

    h_norm_val = calculate_h_norm(omega_new, rho_new, params)

    return SimState(
        time_idx=state.time_idx + 1,
        field=A_new,
        omega=omega_new,
        grad_omega=grad_omega_new,
        h_norm=h_norm_val,
        config_hash=state.config_hash
    )
3. worker/ir_physics/solver.py
Standard JAX scan harness.

Python
"""
worker/ir_physics/solver.py
The Scanning Engine.
"""
import jax
from functools import partial
from .models import SimState, SimParams
from .kernels import step_physics, get_green_function

@partial(jax.jit, static_argnames=['total_steps', 'grid_size'])
def run_simulation_scan(
    initial_state: SimState, 
    params: SimParams, 
    total_steps: int,
    grid_size: int
):
    """
    Executes the full simulation trajectory.
    """
    
    # 1. Precompute static Green's function (FFT)
    splash_green_fn = get_green_function(
        (grid_size, grid_size, grid_size), 
        params.dx, 
        params.sigma_k
    )

    # 2. Define the Scan Body
    def scan_body(carry: SimState, _):
        new_state = step_physics(carry, params, splash_green_fn)
        return new_state, new_state.h_norm

    # 3. Execute Scan
    final_state, h_norm_history = jax.lax.scan(
        scan_body,
        initial_state,
        None,
        length=total_steps
    )
    
    return final_state, h_norm_history
4. worker/ir_physics/stability_envelope.py
NEW FILE: Implements the nonlinear stability mapping logic. This allows you to programmatically find the safe operating regions of the engine.

Python
"""
worker/ir_physics/stability_envelope.py
Tools for mapping the nonlinear stability manifold of the GFL engine.
"""
import jax.numpy as jnp
from .kernels import dt_stability_bound, alpha_critical
from .models import SimParams

def compute_stability_envelope(params: SimParams, rho_range: jnp.ndarray, alpha_range: jnp.ndarray):
    """
    Maps (alpha, rho_max) -> dt_bound
    Returns a matrix where values < current_dt indicate instability.
    """
    dt_map = jnp.zeros((len(alpha_range), len(rho_range)))

    # Loop over ranges (Note: In pure JAX this would be vmapped, 
    # but for analysis/plotting standard loop is fine)
    for i, alpha in enumerate(alpha_range):
        # Create a temp params object with modified alpha
        p_mod = params._replace(alpha=float(alpha))
        
        for j, rho in enumerate(rho_range):
            dt_map = dt_map.at[i, j].set(dt_stability_bound(p_mod, float(rho)))

    return dt_map

def compute_alpha_critical_curve(params: SimParams, rho_range: jnp.ndarray):
    """
    Computes the critical alpha threshold for a range of densities
    given the *current* fixed dt in params.
    """
    curve = []
    for rho in rho_range:
        curve.append(alpha_critical(params, float(rho)))
    return jnp.array(curve)

1. Mathematical Unit Tests (worker/tests/test_gfl_math.py)
This script validates the individual mathematical components. It proves that your jnp.roll operators are functioning correctly on the Torus and that the stability formulas return physical values.

Python
"""
worker/tests/test_gfl_math.py
Unit tests for GFL-RK4 mathematical operators and stability bounds.
Usage: pytest worker/tests/test_gfl_math.py
"""
import pytest
import jax
import jax.numpy as jnp
import numpy as np
from worker.ir_physics import kernels, models

def test_periodic_laplacian_accuracy():
    """
    Verifies that the roll-based Laplacian matches the analytical Laplacian
    for a smooth sine wave on a torus. Accuracy should be O(dx^2).
    """
    N = 64
    L = 2.0 * np.pi
    dx = L / N
    x = jnp.linspace(0, L, N, endpoint=False)
    y = jnp.linspace(0, L, N, endpoint=False)
    z = jnp.linspace(0, L, N, endpoint=False)
    X, Y, Z = jnp.meshgrid(x, y, z, indexing='ij')

    # Test Function: sin(x) + sin(y) + sin(z)
    # Laplacian Analytical: -sin(x) - sin(y) - sin(z) = -Field
    field = jnp.sin(X) + jnp.sin(Y) + jnp.sin(Z)
    analytical_lap = -field

    # Numerical Laplacian
    numerical_lap = kernels.laplacian_periodic(field, dx)

    # Error Metric
    error = jnp.abs(numerical_lap - analytical_lap)
    max_error = jnp.max(error)

    print(f"Max Laplacian Error (N={N}): {max_error}")
    
    # Second order accuracy check: Error should be small (~1e-3 for N=64)
    assert max_error < 0.01, "Laplacian accuracy is insufficient."

def test_gradient_periodic_properties():
    """
    Verifies that gradients are anti-symmetric and periodic.
    """
    N = 32
    field = jax.random.normal(jax.random.PRNGKey(0), (N, N, N))
    dx = 1.0
    
    grads = kernels.get_gradients_periodic(field, dx)
    
    # Check shape
    assert grads.shape == (N, N, N, 3)
    
    # Check mean gradient on periodic domain should be close to 0 (Fundamental Theorem of Calculus on Torus)
    mean_grad = jnp.mean(grads, axis=(0,1,2))
    assert jnp.allclose(mean_grad, 0.0, atol=1e-5), "Gradient integration on torus did not sum to zero."

def test_stability_bound_logic():
    """
    Verifies that the stability bound shrinks as Density increases or Alpha increases.
    """
    params = models.SimParams(
        dt=0.1, epsilon=0.1, alpha=1.0, rho_vac=1.0,
        c1=0.0, c3=0.0, splash_fraction=0.0, sigma_k=1.0, dx=1.0
    )
    
    rho_low = 10.0
    rho_high = 1000.0
    
    bound_low = kernels.dt_stability_bound(params, rho_low)
    bound_high = kernels.dt_stability_bound(params, rho_high)
    
    # Higher density = Stiffer curvature = Lower dt bound
    assert bound_high < bound_low, "Stability bound did not shrink with higher density."
    
    # Check Alpha scaling
    params_high_alpha = params._replace(alpha=2.0)
    bound_alpha = kernels.dt_stability_bound(params_high_alpha, rho_low)
    
    assert bound_alpha < bound_low, "Stability bound did not shrink with higher alpha."

def test_geometry_proxy_clamping():
    """
    Verifies that the geometric proxy clamps correctly to prevent singularity.
    """
    params = models.SimParams(
        dt=0.1, epsilon=0.0, alpha=1.0, rho_vac=1.0,
        c1=0.0, c3=0.0, splash_fraction=0.0, sigma_k=1.0, dx=1.0
    )
    
    # Extreme density (should trigger clamp)
    rho_extreme = jnp.array(1e9)
    omega = kernels.solve_geometry_proxy(rho_extreme, params)
    
    # The kernel clamps omega to min 0.01
    assert omega >= 0.01, "Omega lower bound clamp failed."
    assert omega <= 1.5, "Omega upper bound clamp failed."

if __name__ == "__main__":
    # verification script manually
    try:
        test_periodic_laplacian_accuracy()
        test_gradient_periodic_properties()
        test_stability_bound_logic()
        test_geometry_proxy_clamping()
        print("✅ All Math Unit Tests Passed.")
    except AssertionError as e:
        print(f"❌ Test Failed: {e}")
2. Nonlinear Stability Mapper (worker/validation/map_stability.py)
This script uses your new stability_envelope.py to physically map the safe operating region of the engine. It proves where the "Cliff Edge" of stability is.

Python
"""
worker/validation/map_stability.py
Generates a heatmap of the Stability Envelope.
Maps (Alpha vs Rho_Max) to Safe_DT.
"""
import jax.numpy as jnp
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import seaborn as sns
from worker.ir_physics import stability_envelope, models

def run_mapping():
    print("Mapping Nonlinear Stability Envelope...")
    
    # 1. Setup Parameter Space
    params = models.SimParams(
        dt=0.1, epsilon=0.1, alpha=1.0, rho_vac=1.0,
        c1=0.0, c3=0.0, splash_fraction=0.5, sigma_k=1.0, dx=1.0
    )
    
    # Log-space for density, Linear for Alpha
    rho_range = jnp.logspace(0, 4, 50)  # Density from 1 to 10,000
    alpha_range = jnp.linspace(0.1, 4.0, 50) # Alpha from 0.1 to 4.0
    
    # 2. Compute Envelope
    # dt_map[i, j] corresponds to alpha[i], rho[j]
    dt_map = stability_envelope.compute_stability_envelope(params, rho_range, alpha_range)
    
    # 3. Visualize
    # (If running on headless server, this saves to file)
    plt.figure(figsize=(10, 8))
    sns.heatmap(
        dt_map, 
        xticklabels=5, yticklabels=5,
        cmap="viridis",
        cbar_kws={'label': 'Max Stable Time Step (dt)'}
    )
    
    plt.xlabel("Density (log scale index)")
    plt.ylabel("Alpha Coupling (linear index)")
    plt.title("GFL-RK4 Nonlinear Stability Manifold")
    plt.gca().invert_yaxis() # Standard plot convention
    
    output_path = "stability_manifold.png"
    plt.savefig(output_path)
    print(f"✅ Stability map saved to {output_path}")
    print(f"   - Dark regions require extremely small dt (Stiff/Unstable)")
    print(f"   - Bright regions are stable with larger dt")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    run_mapping()
3. Resolution Invariance Test (worker/validation/check_invariance.py)
This is the critical "Physics vs Artifact" test. It runs the engine at Low Res (N=32) and High Res (N=64) to ensure the physics scales correctly.

Python
"""
worker/validation/check_invariance.py
Verifies that the physics scales correctly with resolution (Grid Invariance).
"""
import jax
import jax.numpy as jnp
from worker.ir_physics import solver, models, kernels

def run_invariance_test():
    print("Running Resolution Invariance Test...")
    
    # Shared Physical Constants
    L_physical = 32.0 # Physical size of the box
    TOTAL_TIME = 20.0 # Physical duration
    
    # --- Run 1: Low Resolution (N=32) ---
    N_low = 32
    dx_low = L_physical / N_low
    # Scaling dt with dx^2 for stability
    dt_low = 0.05 * (dx_low**2) 
    steps_low = int(TOTAL_TIME / dt_low)
    
    print(f"\n--- Low Res Run (N={N_low}, dx={dx_low:.3f}, dt={dt_low:.4f}) ---")
    
    params_low = models.SimParams(
        dt=dt_low, epsilon=0.1, alpha=0.5, rho_vac=1.0,
        c1=0.0, c3=1.0, splash_fraction=0.1, sigma_k=1.0, dx=dx_low
    )
    
    # Init state (Gaussian pulse)
    x = jnp.linspace(0, L_physical, N_low, endpoint=False)
    X, Y, Z = jnp.meshgrid(x, x, x, indexing='ij')
    center = L_physical / 2.0
    field_low = jnp.exp(-((X-center)**2 + (Y-center)**2 + (Z-center)**2)/16.0) + 0j
    
    state_low = models.SimState(
        time_idx=0, field=field_low, 
        omega=jnp.ones_like(field_low), 
        grad_omega=jnp.zeros((*field_low.shape, 3)), 
        h_norm=jnp.array(0.0), config_hash=0
    )
    
    final_low, _ = solver.run_simulation_scan(state_low, params_low, steps_low, N_low, use_adaptive_dt=True)
    
    # --- Run 2: High Resolution (N=64) ---
    N_high = 64
    dx_high = L_physical / N_high
    # dt must scale with dx^2 to maintain same CFL condition
    dt_high = 0.05 * (dx_high**2)
    steps_high = int(TOTAL_TIME / dt_high)
    
    print(f"\n--- High Res Run (N={N_high}, dx={dx_high:.3f}, dt={dt_high:.4f}) ---")
    
    params_high = models.SimParams(
        dt=dt_high, epsilon=0.1, alpha=0.5, rho_vac=1.0,
        c1=0.0, c3=1.0, splash_fraction=0.1, sigma_k=1.0, dx=dx_high
    )
    
    # Init state (Same physical Gaussian, higher sampling)
    x = jnp.linspace(0, L_physical, N_high, endpoint=False)
    X, Y, Z = jnp.meshgrid(x, x, x, indexing='ij')
    field_high = jnp.exp(-((X-center)**2 + (Y-center)**2 + (Z-center)**2)/16.0) + 0j
    
    state_high = models.SimState(
        time_idx=0, field=field_high, 
        omega=jnp.ones_like(field_high), 
        grad_omega=jnp.zeros((*field_high.shape, 3)), 
        h_norm=jnp.array(0.0), config_hash=0
    )
    
    final_high, _ = solver.run_simulation_scan(state_high, params_high, steps_high, N_high, use_adaptive_dt=True)

    # --- Comparison ---
    print("\n--- Invariance metrics ---")
    max_rho_low = jnp.max(jnp.abs(final_low.field)**2)
    max_rho_high = jnp.max(jnp.abs(final_high.field)**2)
    
    print(f"Max Density (Low Res):  {max_rho_low:.4f}")
    print(f"Max Density (High Res): {max_rho_high:.4f}")
    
    diff = jnp.abs(max_rho_low - max_rho_high)
    print(f"Absolute Difference: {diff:.4f}")
    
    if diff < 0.5: # Tolerance depends on dynamics, but shouldn't be massive
        print("✅ Grid Invariance Confirmed (Physics scales correctly)")
    else:
        print("⚠️ Significant Deviation (Check scaling laws)")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    run_invariance_test()

1. Updated worker/worker_v14_sdg.py
This version:

Enables Adaptive DT: Adds a flag to the job schema.

Handles Instability: Detects the -1.0 flag from the kernel and marks the job as FAILED (Instability) instead of SUCCESS.

Computes SDG Mismatch: Runs the spectral solver at the end to quantify how much the algebraic geometry violated the Poisson equation.

Python
import os
import json
import time
import redis
import h5py
import io
import jax
import jax.numpy as jnp
from pydantic import BaseModel, ValidationError
from minio import Minio
from ir_physics import models, solver, kernels

# --- Schemas ---
class SDGParams(BaseModel):
    dt: float
    epsilon: float
    alpha: float
    sigma_k: float
    c1: float
    c3: float
    splash_fraction: float
    dx: float

class JobSchema(BaseModel):
    job_id: str
    params: dict
    grid_size: int = 32
    total_steps: int = 100
    config_hash: str | None = None
    use_adaptive_dt: bool = True  # NEW: Enable stability control by default

class SDGWorker:
    def __init__(self):
        self.redis_host = os.getenv("REDIS_HOST", "localhost")
        self.minio_endpoint = os.getenv("MINIO_ENDPOINT", "localhost:9000")
        self.minio_user = os.getenv("MINIO_ACCESS_KEY", "irer_minio_admin")
        self.minio_pass = os.getenv("MINIO_SECRET_KEY", "irer_minio_password")
        self.worker_id = os.getenv("WORKER_ID", f"worker_{os.getpid()}")
        self.bucket_name = "irer-artifacts"

        self.redis = redis.Redis(host=self.redis_host, port=6379, db=0, decode_responses=True)
        self.minio = Minio(
            self.minio_endpoint,
            access_key=self.minio_user,
            secret_key=self.minio_pass,
            secure=False
        )
        if not self.minio.bucket_exists(self.bucket_name):
            self.minio.make_bucket(self.bucket_name)

    def compute_config_hash(self, params):
        import hashlib
        s = json.dumps(params, sort_keys=True)
        return hashlib.sha256(s.encode()).hexdigest()

    def run(self):
        print(f"[{self.worker_id}] Ready. Waiting for jobs...")
        while True:
            job = self.redis.blpop("jobs:sdg_physics", timeout=10)
            if not job: continue
            _, payload_str = job
            try:
                self.process_job(payload_str)
            except Exception as e:
                print(f"[{self.worker_id}] CRITICAL FAILURE: {e}")
                self.redis.lpush("dlq:sdg_physics", payload_str)

    def process_job(self, payload_str):
        try:
            # 1. Validation & Setup
            job_dict = json.loads(payload_str)
            job = JobSchema(**job_dict)
            params = SDGParams(**job.params)

            print(f"[{self.worker_id}] >>> Starting Job: {job.job_id}")

            # Config Integrity Check
            calculated_hash = self.compute_config_hash(job.params)
            if job.config_hash and job.config_hash != calculated_hash:
                print(f"[{self.worker_id}] WARNING: Config Hash Mismatch!")

            # 2. JAX Simulation
            sim_params = models.SimParams(
                dt=params.dt, epsilon=params.epsilon, alpha=params.alpha,
                sigma_k=params.sigma_k, c1=params.c1, c3=params.c3,
                splash_fraction=params.splash_fraction, dx=params.dx
            )

            # Initialize with Gaussian noise
            key = jax.random.PRNGKey(42)
            initial_field = jax.random.normal(key, shape=(job.grid_size, job.grid_size, job.grid_size), dtype=jnp.complex64)
            
            # Initial geometry setup
            rho_init = jnp.abs(initial_field)**2
            omega_init = kernels.solve_geometry_proxy(rho_init, sim_params)
            grad_omega_init = kernels.get_gradients_periodic(omega_init, sim_params.dx)

            initial_state = models.SimState(
                time_idx=0,
                field=initial_field,
                omega=omega_init,
                grad_omega=grad_omega_init,
                h_norm=jnp.array(0.0),
                config_hash=0
            )

            print(f"[{self.worker_id}] Solving (Adaptive DT: {job.use_adaptive_dt})...")
            start_time = time.time()
            
            final_state, h_norm_history = solver.run_simulation_scan(
                initial_state, 
                sim_params, 
                job.total_steps, 
                job.grid_size,
                use_adaptive_dt=job.use_adaptive_dt,
                fully_coupled_geometry=False
            )
            
            # Block until ready to catch JAX errors
            max_h_norm = float(jnp.max(h_norm_history).block_until_ready())
            duration = time.time() - start_time

            # 3. Post-Run Diagnostics
            
            # A. Check for Instability Flag (-1.0 from kernel)
            status = "SUCCESS"
            failure_reason = None
            if max_h_norm < 0: 
                status = "FAILED"
                failure_reason = "Numerical Instability (NaN/Inf Detected)"
                max_h_norm = 999.9 # Normalize for logging

            # B. SDG Spectral Comparison (Proxy vs Elliptic)
            if status == "SUCCESS":
                rho_final = jnp.abs(final_state.field)**2
                omega_elliptic = kernels.solve_geometry_sdg_spectral(rho_final, params.alpha, params.dx)
                # Compute RMS difference
                sdg_mismatch = float(jnp.sqrt(jnp.mean((final_state.omega - omega_elliptic)**2)))
            else:
                sdg_mismatch = -1.0

            # 4. Upload Artifact
            self.upload_artifact(job.job_id, final_state, h_norm_history, job.params)

            # 5. Report Result
            result_payload = {
                "job_id": job.job_id,
                "status": status,
                "failure_reason": failure_reason,
                "artifact_url": f"s3://{self.bucket_name}/{job.job_id}.h5",
                "metrics": {
                    "max_h_norm": max_h_norm, 
                    "sdg_mismatch": sdg_mismatch,
                    "duration": duration
                }
            }
            self.redis.lpush("results:physics", json.dumps(result_payload))
            print(f"[{self.worker_id}] Finished {job.job_id}: {status} (Mismatch: {sdg_mismatch:.4f})")

        except Exception as e:
            print(f"[{self.worker_id}] UNKNOWN ERROR: {e}")
            # Push back to DLQ if possible or log error
            self.redis.lpush("dlq:sdg_physics", payload_str)

    def upload_artifact(self, job_id, state, history, params):
        bio = io.BytesIO()
        with h5py.File(bio, 'w') as f:
            f.create_dataset("rho", data=jnp.abs(state.field)**2)
            f.create_dataset("omega", data=state.omega)
            f.create_dataset("h_norm_history", data=history)
            for k, v in params.items():
                f.attrs[k] = v
        bio.seek(0)
        self.minio.put_object(
            self.bucket_name, f"{job_id}.h5", bio, bio.getbuffer().nbytes,
            content_type="application/x-hdf5"
        )

if __name__ == "__main__":
    worker = SDGWorker()
    worker.run()
2. Stability Driver (validation/map_stability.py)
This script uses the stability_envelope module to generate the heatmap. It corresponds to the empty file in your bundle.

Python
"""
validation/map_stability.py
Driver script to map the Nonlinear Stability Envelope.
Run this to see where the engine breaks.
"""
import os
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import seaborn as sns
import jax.numpy as jnp
from worker.ir_physics import stability_envelope, models

def run_mapping():
    print("Mapping Nonlinear Stability Envelope...")
    
    # 1. Setup Base Parameters
    params = models.SimParams(
        dt=0.1, epsilon=0.1, alpha=1.0, rho_vac=1.0,
        c1=0.0, c3=0.0, splash_fraction=0.5, sigma_k=1.0, dx=1.0
    )
    
    # 2. Define Search Space
    # Log-space for density (1 to 10,000)
    rho_range = jnp.logspace(0, 4, 50)  
    # Linear for Alpha (0.1 to 4.0)
    alpha_range = jnp.linspace(0.1, 4.0, 50) 
    
    # 3. Compute Envelope
    # dt_map[i, j] corresponds to alpha[i], rho[j]
    print("Computing dt bounds across parameter manifold...")
    dt_map = stability_envelope.compute_stability_envelope(params, rho_range, alpha_range)
    
    # 4. Visualize
    plt.figure(figsize=(10, 8))
    sns.heatmap(
        dt_map, 
        xticklabels=10, yticklabels=10,
        cmap="viridis",
        cbar_kws={'label': 'Max Stable Time Step (dt)'}
    )
    
    # Label formatting
    plt.xlabel("Max Density (log scale index)")
    plt.ylabel("Alpha Coupling (linear index)")
    plt.title("GFL-RK4 Nonlinear Stability Manifold")
    plt.gca().invert_yaxis()
    
    output_path = "stability_manifold.png"
    plt.savefig(output_path)
    print(f"✅ Stability map saved to {output_path}")
    print(f"   - Dark regions = Instability (Small dt required)")
    print(f"   - Bright regions = Stable (Large dt allowed)")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    run_mapping()

report 1: ""Defining the Canonical Code Platform (CCP): A Framework for Grounded Agentic Logic



1. Executive Definition and Project Relevance



In the current landscape of large-scale agentic deployment, operating within complex, partially observable environments requires an architectural "Canonical" reference point. Without a standardized logic layer, autonomous systems succumb to the entropy of environmental noise, resulting in "mismatched execution" where agent behavior diverges from intended outcomes. The Canonical Code Platform (CCP) is a non-parametric reasoning backbone designed to stabilize agentic logic by prioritizing internal state modeling over ephemeral "thought-action" loops.



Architecturally, the CCP serves as a stabilizing layer that anchors agentic behavior in what systems ethics defines as the "constants of the human predicament"—the persistent requirements of a task, such as food, shelter, or specific operational goals—rather than the "variable factors" of shifting environmental context. By placing the agent behind a "technological veil of ignorance" regarding noisy, irrelevant historical data, the CCP forces reasoning to rely on the grounded relationship between the current internal belief state and the ultimate task goal. This ensuring of impartial, goal-consistent logic is the foundation of the platform's reliability.



2. Strategic Purpose: Resolving the Ungrounded Thought Crisis



The CCP was engineered to solve the "Ungrounded Thought Problem" inherent in frameworks like ReAct. In these systems, reasoning steps often become disconnected from the actual state of the world, biasing the action probability distribution toward "hallucinated" outcomes.



Performance Analysis: The Entropy Fallacy



Our analysis of the ReAct baseline reveals a dangerous "confidence gap." While a NoThinking agent exhibits a mean action distribution entropy of 1.23 (reflecting high uncertainty), the ReAct framework reduces this to 0.30. However, this 0.30 figure represents "ungrounded confidence." The agent becomes highly focused on a specific action path, but that path is frequently based on a reasoning error that ignores historical context or goal misalignment. The CCP aims to maintain this focus while ensuring it is fundamentally grounded.



Problem vs. Canonical Solution



Feature Short-sighted Reasoning (ReAct) Goal-Aligned Reflection (ReflAct)

Reasoning Focus Immediate "next-step" thinking (c'_t = c_t \oplus \tau_t). Structured relation between state and goal (k \in K).

Exploitation Leads to "Unnecessary Exploitation" (redundant loops). Eliminates redundancy via belief-state tracking.

Execution High risk of "Mismatched Execution" (false assumptions). Grounded selection via non-parametric modeling.

Grounding Relies on external parametric knowledge (WKM). Redesigns reasoning within the internal backbone.



The CCP targets three specific reliability standards:



1. Grounded Focus: Transforming the 0.30 entropy level from "blind confidence" into "informed precision."

2. Safety Invariance: Introducing zero unique failure modes; the platform only fails in scenarios where the base model lacks the inherent capacity to solve the task.

3. Exploration Efficiency: Reducing the total number of reasoning steps by adapting strategy based on environmental cues rather than repeating failed actions.



3. Expected Capabilities: Internal State and Goal Alignment



To achieve grounded logic, the CCP utilizes a Reflection Space K, a structured representation that explicitly encodes the agent’s internal belief state (M) and the overarching task goal (G).



Belief-State Modeling



The platform tracks a "sufficient statistic of history," maintaining a rigorous representation of the world that prevents common failures. For instance, in "boiling lead" tasks (ScienceWorld), ungrounded agents often assume they possess a material (lead) simply because they located it, leading to a hallucinated "move" action. The CCP’s belief-state modeling ensures the agent acknowledges it must first "take" the item before it can "possess" it.



The Action Demodulator: SDR Metaphor



The CCP functions as an Action Demodulator, analogous to a Software Defined Radio (SDR) 200 system used in transportation infrastructure. Just as an SDR simultaneously processes parallel data paths of different frequencies and modulation types—such as ITCNET, MBNET, and ATCS—the CCP demodulates diverse "logical frequencies" (environmental observations and task protocols) into a single, grounded action. This multi-channel adaptability allows the agent to maintain the "constant" signal of the goal while filtering the "noise" of variable environmental factors.



4. Methodological Framework: The ReflAct Process



The CCP’s primary engine is the ReflAct process. It replaces the standard instruction "Thought: [Next Action]" with a high-rigor directive: "You should first reflect on the agent’s state in relation to the task goal, and then output the action."



Step-by-Step Logic Flow



1. Observation Acquisition: Integration of environmental data into the belief state M.

2. Goal-State Reflection: Synthesizing the relationship k = [M, G] to determine if the current state is moving toward or away from the goal.

3. Action Selection: Re-weighting the policy \pi_{act} based on the grounded reflection k.



Prototypical Reasoning Comparison (ALFWorld/Jericho)



* ReAct (Short-sighted Planning):

  * Observation: "Cabinet 1 contains a soapbottle."

  * Thought: "I put the soapbottle back. Now I can search for soap. I'll go to cabinet 1 again."

  * Outcome: Unnecessary Exploitation. The agent loops back to a location it has already cleared, ultimately failing.

* ReflAct (Adaptive Strategy):

  * Observation: "The barrels are rotten staves... you see a pewter mug."

  * Reflection: "I have been searching for a mug. I previously checked the tables and chairs without success. The cellar is a promising storage area, and I have now located the item essential for the task."

  * Outcome: Task Success. The agent adapts its exploration strategy based on prior search failures and environmental cues.



This process is primed using One-Shot Examples, activating the internal reasoning capabilities of backbones like Llama-3.1-8B or GPT-4o without requiring the architectural overhead of external knowledge modules.



5. Performance Benchmarks and Reliability Standards



The CCP, powered by ReflAct, demonstrates statistically significant improvements across diverse benchmarks. By fundamentally redesigning the reasoning backbone, the platform achieves the following success rate increases over the "NoThinking" baseline:



* ALFWorld: 77.9% improvement (reaching 60.5% success on Llama-3.1-8B).

* ScienceWorld: 25.9% improvement.

* Jericho: 101.1% improvement.



Architectural Robustness



The platform is not a fragile "prompt hack." Experiments with instruction paraphrasing and example modification show only minor fluctuations in performance, confirming that the CCP represents a stable, canonical architectural choice.



Ethical Foundation and "Safe Operation"



From a systems ethics perspective, the CCP reduces the risk of autonomous systems making harmful decisions based on ungrounded reasoning. By ensuring that every action is preceded by a reflection on the "state-goal relation," the platform reduces the hallucinated action rate. Furthermore, as shown in the failure ratio diagrams of the ReflAct source, the CCP introduces zero unique failure modes (1% and 0% unique failures for Llama and GPT-4o respectively). It operates as a "safe" reasoning framework, fulfilling the ethical mandate to create trustworthy AI systems that remain synchronized with human objectives in the most complex, partially observable environments.
